This week&rsquo;s list includes <strong>JPMorgan</strong>&nbsp;(NYSE:&nbsp;<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/JPM">JPM</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=JPM">Free Report</a>) and&nbsp;<strong>Citigroup</strong>&nbsp;(NYSE:&nbsp;<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/C">C</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=C">Free Report</a>).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">To see more earnings analysis, visit <a href="https://at.zacks.com/?id=3207">https://at.zacks.com/?id=3207</a>.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Every day, Zacks.com makes their Bull Stock of the Day available, free of charge. <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=PR&amp;ADID=PR_EP_PFP">To see it, click here</a>.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Are Bank Stock Gains Sustainable?</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It has been a tough ride for bank stocks this year, with the industry unable to sustain the post-election momentum after mid-February 2017. As a group, bank stocks didn&rsquo;t do much from mid-February through early September. But they have experienced dramatic gains since September 8th, with a number of major bank stocks trading at or near their highs for the year.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">This lack of sustained performance notwithstanding, the industry remains an integral part of the &lsquo;Trump Trade,&rsquo; with the industry handily outperforming the broader market since&nbsp;November 7th.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The chart below plots the performance of the Zacks Major Banks industry relative to the S&amp;P 500 Index since the elections. Please note that the Zacks Major Banks industry includes all the money-center banks and big regionals that kick-off the Q3 earnings season for the industry on Thursday October 12th with the&nbsp;<strong>JPMorgan</strong>&nbsp;(NYSE: <a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/JPM" target="_blank"><strong>JPM</strong></a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=JPM">Free Report</a>) and&nbsp;<strong>Citigroup</strong>&nbsp;(NYSE: <a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/C" target="_blank"><strong>C</strong></a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=C">Free Report</a>) results.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">What this shows is that stocks in the Zacks Major Banks industry are up +28.5% since&nbsp;November 7th, outperforming the S&amp;P 500 index&rsquo;s +19.2% gain in that same time period. The broader Finance sector, of which the Major Banks industry is big part, accounting for roughly 40% of the sector&rsquo;s total earnings, is up +24% since&nbsp;November 7th.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Bank stocks are up more than +8% over the past month, roughly double the S&amp;P 500&rsquo;s performance in that time period. Optimism about tax policy changes appears to be a contributing factor to the group&rsquo;s recent momentum. It&rsquo;s hard to be overly optimistic about substance and timing of a policy legislation given the healthcare experience, but lower corporate taxes will be highly beneficial to the banking industry. As large as many of these big industry players are, they are still primarily domestic oriented businesses that stand to benefit from lower corporate tax rates (just as small-cap stocks do).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Trends in treasury yields have an outsized bearing on bank stocks since they are a big driver of bank margins. You can see this correlation in the year-to-date stock market performance of the industry relative to the 10-year treasury yield, with the industry&rsquo;s bounce since September 8th coinciding with the most recent bottoming in the treasury yields.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Whether the group&rsquo;s recent outperformance over the past month is a function of treasury yields, or hopes of tax law changes or both, it&rsquo;s foundations appear shaky. Tax cuts would be good for banks, but who knows when or whether they will arrive. Treasury yields have been unable to cross the 2.4% level at the high end, though they reached that level three times since March this year. They are heading to that level again, with the 10-year yield getting a modest bump from the stronger-looking wage growth numbers in the otherwise &lsquo;noisy&rsquo; September jobs report. But if recent history has to repeat itself, then we should look for yields to start moving down after getting close to the 2.4% level. &nbsp;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">With these two supports for the group less than credible, let&rsquo;s take a look at the group&rsquo;s earnings potential to see if we can find support there.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>What Are Banks Expected to Report in Q3?</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Bank earnings failed to impress in the Q2 earnings season and all of the factors that weighed on Q2 results remained in place in Q3 as well, keeping expectations in check. Net interest margin benefited from the June Fed rate hike, but that incremental gain likely got offset by persistent deceleration in loan growth and soft trading revenues. The September quarter is traditionally a seasonally weak period on the capital markets front. This year&rsquo;s Q3 was mixed, with stable fixed income trading flows and positive fixed income underwriting trends offset by weak equity trading volumes and issuance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">What all of this means is that bank stocks could benefit from low and relatively easy-to-beat expectations.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Total Q3 earnings for the Zacks Major Banks industry are expected to be down -5.1% from the same period last year on +2.2% higher revenues. This would follow +10% earnings growth in Q2 and +19.4% growth in 2017 Q2. JP Morgan and Citigroup, on deck to release Q3 results&nbsp;on Thursday, are expected to report -6.6% and -8.2% lower earnings from the year-earlier level, respectively.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The table below shows the sector&rsquo;s Q3 earnings growth expectations at the medium-industry level contrasted with estimates for the following four quarters and actual results for the preceding three periods.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Please note that the Major Banks industry, of which JPMorgan, Citigroup and others are part, accounts for roughly 45% of the sector&rsquo;s total earnings (insurance is the second biggest earnings contributor, accounting for about 25% of the total). The insurance industry has been hard hit by this year&rsquo;s very active and impactful hurricane season, with estimates for insurers taking a big hit since the quarter got underway.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">We discussed the hurricane impact in our weekly Earnings Trends report here &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;<a href="https://www.zacks.com/commentary/131005/the-earnings-impact-of-hurricanes" target="_blank">Earnings Impact of Hurricanes</a></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Expectations for Q3</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Total Q3 earnings are expected to be up +2.2% from the same period last year on +5% higher revenues. This would follow +11.1% earnings growth in 2017 Q2 on +5.5%, the second quarter in a row of double-digit earnings growth.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Estimates for Q3 came down as the quarter unfolded, with the current +2.2% growth down from +6.3% at the end of June.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Please note that while Q3 estimates have followed the well traversed path that we have been seeing consistently over the last few years, the magnitude of negative revisions nevertheless compares favorably to other periods. In other words, Q3 estimates have come down, but they haven&rsquo;t come down by as much.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In terms of sector focus, the strongest growth in Q3 is coming from the Energy sector which benefits from easy comparisons. Excluding the Energy sector, the aggregate growth pace drops to +0.4% from +2.2%. The Conglomerate sector is the only other sectors with double-digit growth rates. Earnings growth is also strong for the Technology sector, with total earnings for the sector expected to be up +9.7% on +6.7% higher revenues.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">On the negative side, Q3 earnings are expected to be below the year-earlier level for 8 of the 16 Zacks sectors, with double-digit declines for the Transportation, Aerospace, Basic Materials and Autos sectors.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>About Zacks</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Zacks.com is a property of Zacks Investment Research, Inc., which was formed in 1978. Analyst Blog Highlights: Seiko Epson, Honda Motor and Park-Ohio Holdings', 'content': [{'base': u'http://feed.zacks.com/commentary/AllStories/rss', 'type': u'text/html', 'value': u'<p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>For Immediate Release</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Chicago, IL &ndash; October 09, 2017 &ndash; Zacks.com announces the list of stocks featured in the Analyst Blog. Every day the Zacks Equity Research analysts discuss the latest news and events impacting stocks and the financial markets. Stocks recently featured in the blog include&nbsp;<strong><strong>Seiko Epson Corp. </strong></strong>(OTCMKTS:<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/SEKEY">SEKEY</a>&nbsp;<strong>&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=SEKEY">Free Report</a></strong>)<strong>, </strong><strong>Honda Motor </strong>(NYSE:<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/HMC">HMC</a>&nbsp;<strong>&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=HMC">Free Report</a></strong>) and <strong>Park-Ohio Holdings Corp. </strong>(Nasdaq:<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/PKOH">PKOH</a>&nbsp;<strong>&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=PKOH">Free Report</a></strong>).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Today, Zacks is promoting its \'\'Buy\'\' stock recommendations. <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=PR&amp;ADID=PR_AB_PFP">Get #1Stock of the Day pick for free</a><strong>. </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Here are highlights from Friday&rsquo;s Analyst Blog: </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>What Is the Greatest Threat to Our Nation?</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><em>The following is an excerpt from Zacks Chief Strategist John Blank&rsquo;s full <a href="https://www.zacks.com/ZER/zer_get_pdf.php?r=H7309958370&amp;t=&amp;adid=zp_article_marketstrategy">Oct Market Strategy report</a></em><strong><em>To access the full PDF,</em></strong><em>&nbsp;<a href="https://www.zacks.com/ZER/zer_get_pdf.php?r=H7309958370&amp;t=&amp;adid=zp_article_marketstrategy"><strong>click here.</strong></a></em></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>I. U.S. Markets </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">I am going to start this U.S. overview with Eurozone budget data. Eurozone data, you ask? Shouldn&rsquo;t that be in the global overview? Not this month. This month, I will have the USA and Mainland China trade date in the global section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">What am I thinking harder about? The big policy issues most investors to this publication would like to know more about: U.S. trade and tax decisions.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">What this PhD economist needs to do first? Cover tax changes. To start, I don&rsquo;t know much of what is going to actually happen on the Federal budget. The House and Senate both must approve a finalized tax plan.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Tax plans come with joint decisions on personal and business taxes, debt financed spending, and revenue sent to Federal programs to fund needed operations -- like national defense, Medicare, and interest on the huge accrued debt. That&rsquo;s where the rubber meets the runway.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">A core matter, then, concerns annual Macroeconomic Balances. I want to share more on that in this letter. There&rsquo;s a logical structure. Most of you are not aware of it. That is the relationship trade balances and their financial sister -- current account balances -- have with Federal budget balances. You cannot violate this.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">All economies -- regardless of size -- function under Macroeconomic Identities.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(1) Aggregate Demand (Spending) = Aggregate Supply (Output), which implies</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Consumption(C) + Investment (I) + Government (G) + Net Exports&nbsp; (NX) = Y</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) C + I + G + Exports = Domestic Production of Goods and Services + Imports</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Below: The latest Consensus Economics macro balances for the Eurozone.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Study this table of twin balances closely. See the relationships? Macro Identities predict.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Tight countries with bigger Budget Surpluses (the Netherlands, Germany &amp; Ireland) run bigger Current Account Surpluses (identical to Trade Surpluses). Loose countries at the bottom (France, Spain, Belgium, Portugal &amp; Italy) run the largest Budget Deficits. The identical countries also accrue the biggest Trade Deficits.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>This is a key point I want to make -- on the USA -- and any other country. </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><em>The bigger your Federal budget deficit, the bigger is your national trade deficit. </em></p><p style="text-align: justify;">I will re-state that final identity/equality. Closely inspect this key relationship:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Consumption + Investment + Government + Exports = Domestic Output + Imports</p><p style="text-align: justify;">When the USA -- or any other country -- is at full employment (4.2% in an unemployment rate is clean evidence of that), running a Federal deficit means over-spending on the ability of the domestic economy to supply the excess demand&nbsp; -- created by the visible excess seen in government budgets</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In times of deep stress -- like a recession or depression in private domestic spending -- John Maynard Keynes in the 1930s argued very effectively. This was a good idea. Get the Federal government to spend, when the private consumer and businesses cannot. That is persuasive. Running and asking for enlarged Federal budget deficits in times of deep private macro stress is forever called &ldquo;Keynesian.&rdquo;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">However, what about an economy that is at full employment? That will mean internal domestic spending, however created, has fully engaged the capacity of the domestic economy to supply it.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">At full employment of domestic resources, any Federal overspending is balanced by production shipped in from abroad (aka Imports). That means this: Larger Federal Budget problems must lead <u>directly</u> to larger Federal Trade Deficits.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">So what, you say?</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Realize: the current USA Federal government is attempting to deal with lowering trade deficits. It is re-negotiating trade deals with Canada, Mexico and Mainland China, among others. Then, the same USA Federal government proposes to increase the Federal budget deficit with tax cuts?</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><em><strong>Ensuing larger Federal budget deficits will surely DRIVE UP the U.S. trade deficit!</strong></em></p><p style="text-align: justify;">I restated it. Because that&rsquo;s a BIG point.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is an undisputable one, from both the point of view of Macro Identities and the recent macro data I showed you from the Eurozone (or any other sovereign for the matter).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">If you want to cut your overall trade deficit, you MUST CUT your budget deficit!</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Why USA politicians try and violate Macro Identities? I do not know.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>II. Global Markets </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">For a Global Outlook, I will present the freshest trade data for the USA and China.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In 2016, the U.S. exported $1.45T and imported $2.19T, leaving a trade deficit of $735B. The U.S. had an $18.6T economy. The trade deficit in % of annual GDP is then -3.95%.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In 2016, in comparison, Mainland China was nearly a mirror image. China exported $2.1T and imported $1.59T, leaving a surplus of $510B. China had an $11.2T economy. The trade surplus in % terms of annual GDP is +4.5%.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The US-China mirror image is no artifact of statistics. It is real. Also pay attention to the statistics on the US&rsquo;s major trading partners. The US runs chronic trade deficits with ALL of its major trading partners, sans our mother in history, the United Kingdom.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><em><strong>What&rsquo;s my big point? Our Federal budget deficit creates our overall trade deficit! </strong></em>U.S. general government borrowing/lending is -4.4% of GDP in 2016. Now, consult the trading partners of China. Lo and behold, Hong Kong and the US see these huge trade surpluses.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Hong Kong is an entrep&ocirc;t.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An&nbsp;<strong>entrep&ocirc;t</strong>&nbsp;or trans-shipment port is a port, city, or trading post where merchandise may be imported, stored or traded, usually to be exported again. These commercial cities are spawned due to the growth of long-distance trade.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Japan, Germany, South Korea and Taiwan? All of these high-income countries currently import much more than they export to China. Really!!! They don&rsquo;t display the US story, at all. It&rsquo;s the reverse.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Current Republican Senator from Tennessee Bob Corker, and a member of the Senate Budget Committee, summed up this situation succinctly:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">&ldquo;<em>I think the greatest threat to our nation is us. The way we handle our finances, we as a nation are the greatest threat to our nation. It&rsquo;s not ISIS. It&rsquo;s not North Korea. It&rsquo;s not ascendant China. It&rsquo;s not Russia. We are the greatest threat</em>.&rdquo;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">&nbsp;--Sept. 29<sup>th</sup>, 2017</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>III. Zacks October Sector/Industry/Company Telescope</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Fall is the season. Sector leaders are clear.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is no surprise to see Info Tech lead. The global economy is heating up. A pro-cyclical domestic bid is on, too, shown by Very Attractive Consumer Discretionary and Industrial sectors. Health Care stays Attractive.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">U.S. jobs are plentiful and stock markets are moving up.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>(1) Info Tech </strong>is, once again, a Very Attractive Sector. The Semiconductors lead, and Electronics is tops. Computer-Software-Services, and Misc. Tech are good.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Top Zacks #1 Rank (STRONG BUY): Seiko Epson Corp. </strong>(OTCMKTS:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/SEKEY">SEKEY</a> <strong>&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=SEKEY">Free Report</a></strong>)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>(2) Consumer Discretionary </strong>stays a Very Attractive Sector. <strong>Alaska Air Group</strong> (NYSE:<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/ALK">ALK</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <a style="text-align: justify;">Link: <a href="https://www.zacks.com/commentary/131256/will-the-ride-get-bumpier-for-airline-stocks">https://www.zacks.com/commentary/131256/will-the-ride-get-bumpier-for-airline-stocks</a></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is a well-documented fact that stocks in the airline space have been plagued by multiple headwinds like weather-related disruptions, pricing issues and high costs. The turbulence in the sector is largely responsible for the NYSE ARCA Airline Index declining 2.5% over the last three months. With Q3 earnings season coming up, the ongoing turbulence may result in airlines performing disappointingly. Let&rsquo;s delve into the details.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Harvey, Irma Ground Airlines - Q3 Unit Revenue Views Cut</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Harvey, which wreaked havoc on America&rsquo;s fourth-largest city, Houston, with heavy rainfall, has negatively impacted airline operations and caused multiple flight cancellations. In fact, air travel was hurt with two Houston airports, George Bush Intercontinental Airport (IAH) and William P. Hobby Airport (HOU), <a href="https://www.bizjournals.com/houston/news/2017/08/30/southwest-cancels-more-flights-houston-airports.html?ana=yahoo&amp;yptr=yahoo">reportedly</a> remaining closed for a few days (since the noon of Aug 27) due to Harvey-induced heavy rainfall. The airports are operational now.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>United Continental Holdings&nbsp;</strong>(NYSE:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/UAL">UAL</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=UAL">Free Report</a>), the parent company of United Airlines, was the worst hit, as Houston is the carrier&rsquo;s second-largest hub. In September 2017, company trimmed its views with respect to pre-tax margin and passenger revenue per available seat mile (PRASM: a key measure of unit revenue) for the third quarter mainly due to Harvey. The carrier now expects PRASM to decline between 3% and 5% year over year (the earlier guidance provided in July was +1% to - 1%).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In fact, Harvey has impacted the third-quarter PRASM to the tune of approximately 150 basis points. The carrier now expects pre-tax margin between 8% and 10% (previous guidance was 12.5% and 14.5%).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Spirit Airlines&nbsp;</strong>(Nasdaq:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/SAVE">SAVE</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=SAVE">Free Report</a>), which also has significant exposure to Houston, expects its top line to shrink to the tune of approximately $8.5 million in the third quarter due to the natural calamity. Currently, Spirit Airlines anticipates total revenue per available seat mile (TRASM) to decline between 7% and 8.5% (the previous guidance was 2% and 4%). In fact, per the company, 100 basis points of the trimmed guidance can be attributed to the negative impact of Harvey. Also, aggressive competitive pricing in its key markets contributed to the bleak forecast.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Southwest Airlines&nbsp;</strong>(NYSE:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/LUV">LUV</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=LUV">Free Report</a>), which had to call off approximately 2,800 flights due to Harvey, now expects operating revenue per available seat mile (RASM) for the third quarter in the range of down 1% to slightly up, on a year-over-year basis. The metric was earlier projected to increase approximately 1% from the year-ago quarter.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Close on the heels of Harvey, came another natural calamity, Irma, which also hurt airline operations. <strong>American Airlines Group</strong> (Nasdaq:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/AAL">AAL</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=AAL">Free Report</a>), which has significant exposure to Florida including its hub at Miami International Airport, had to cancel multiple flights due to Irma. The natural calamity also caused it to trim its third-quarter TRASM view.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>High Costs Likely to Hurt Q3</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">With labor deals in vogue in the aviation space, labor costs have escalated, thereby hurting the bottom lines in the last few quarters. The picture is likely to be no different in the third quarter.&nbsp; For example, labor costs shot up significantly at <strong>Alaska Air Group</strong> (NYSE:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/ALK">ALK</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=ALK">Free Report</a>) following the amendment to the pay-related pilots&rsquo; contract at its subsidiary, Horizon Air.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Following the agreement, the company&nbsp;expects third-quarter cost per available seat mile (excluding fuel and other special items) between 8 cents and 8.05 cents. You can see&nbsp;<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/buy-list/?ADID=zp_1link&amp;ICID=zpi%20_1link" title="blocked::https://www.zacks.com/stocks/buy-list/?ADID=zp_1link&amp;ICID=zpi _1link"><strong>the complete list of today&rsquo;s Zacks #1 Rank (Strong Buy) stocks here</strong></a>.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Moreover, increasing fuel costs do not bode well for airlines. Oil prices are currently hovering around the $50-a-barrel mark, way higher than the lows of around $26 a barrel touched in February last year. The rise in fuel costs, which again may be Harvey induced, are also likely to distort the Q3 earnings picture for airlines.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Strong Stocks that Should Be in the News</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Many are little publicized and fly under the Wall Street radar. the basis of its sales and earnings numbers. These, however, may not be enough. Sometimes, a stock gets a boost if these numbers climb year over year or surpass estimates in a particular quarter. This will definitely be a great opportunity for a short horizon investor to cash in on. But if you seek long-term returns, investments backed only by sales and earnings numbers may not yield the desired results.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">A critical analysis of a company&rsquo;s financial background is a prerequisite for an informed investment decision. Here, coverage ratios that determine whether a company is sound enough to meet its financial obligations play a crucial role. The higher the ratio, the better it is. The focus of this article is on &ldquo;Interest Coverage&rdquo;, which is one such ratio.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><em><u>Interest Coverage Ratio = Earnings before Interest &amp; Taxes (EBIT) divided by Interest Expense</u></em>.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Why Interest Coverage Ratio?</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Interest Coverage Ratio is used to determine how effectively a company can pay the interest charges on its debt.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Debt, which is crucial for most of the companies to finance operations, comes at a cost called interest. Interest expense has a direct bearing on the profitability of a company and its creditworthiness depends on how effectively it meets interest obligations. Therefore, Interest Coverage Ratio is one of the important criteria to factor in before making any investment decision.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Interest Coverage Ratio suggests the number of times the interest could be paid from earnings and also gauges the margin of safety a firm carries for paying interest.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An interest coverage ratio lower than 1.0 implies that the company is unable to fulfill its interest obligations and could default on repaying debt. A company that is capable of generating earnings well above its interest expense can withstand financial hardships. Definitely, one should also track the company&rsquo;s past performance to determine whether the interest coverage ratio has improved or worsened over a period of time.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>The Winning Strategy</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Apart from having an Interest Coverage Ratio that is more than the industry average, adding a favorable Zacks Rank and a <a href="https://www.zacks.com/style-scores-education/">VGM Score</a> of A or B to your search criteria should lead to better results.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Interest Coverage Ratio greater than X-Industry Median</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Price greater than or equal to 5: </strong>The stocks must all be trading at a minimum of $5 or higher.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>5-Year Historical EPS Growth (%) greater than X-Industry Median:</strong> Stocks that have a strong EPS growth history.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Projected EPS Growth (%)</strong><strong> greater than X-Industry Median: </strong>This is the projected EPS growth over the next three to five years. Release</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Chicago, IL &ndash; October 9, 2017 &ndash; Today, Zacks Equity Research discusses the Industry: Airlines, Part 2, including <strong>Delta Air Lines</strong> (NYSE:<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/DAL">DAL</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/UAL">UAL</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=UAL">Free Report</a>), <strong>American Airlines Group</strong> (Nasdaq:<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/AAL">AAL</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=AAL">Free Report</a>), <strong>GOL Linhas</strong> (NYSE:<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/GOL">GOL</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=GOL">Free Report</a>) and <strong>Ryanair Holdings</strong> (Nasdaq:<a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/RYAAY">RYAAY</a>&nbsp;&ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=RYAAY">Free Report</a>).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Industry: Airlines, Part 2</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Link: <a href="https://www.zacks.com/commentary/131251/airlines-still-worth-considering-here39s-why">https://www.zacks.com/commentary/131251/airlines-still-worth-considering-here39s-why</a></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Even though it is true that airline stocks are being confronted with multiple headwinds, all is not lost. There exist a few bright spots that still make investment in airline stocks worthwhile. Let&rsquo;s delve into the details.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Oil Still Below $55 = Financial Prosperity</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Despite the recent rally, oil prices are still hovering around the $50-a-barrel mark, a long way off the highs of mid-2014 when the commodity had traded in excess of $100 a barrel. As fuel costs represent one of the largest input costs for airline companies, the lower the oil prices, the better it is for sector participants. Lower oil prices imply greater financial well-being for airlines by virtue of massive savings.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Financial prosperity is reflected in the fact that the likes of <strong>Delta Air Lines</strong> (NYSE:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/DAL">DAL</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=DAL">Free Report</a>) have hiked their respective dividend payouts this year. Carriers have also indulged in share buybacks, which is more proof of their solid financial health.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Riding on balance sheet strength, some carriers have shelled out impressive amounts to employees as part of their profit-sharing programs. Additionally, the robust financial health of most domestic carriers has prompted them to invest substantially in improving the flying experience for travelers, in a bid to stay afloat in the competitive airline space. For example, United Airlines, the wholly owned subsidiary of <strong>United Continental Holdings</strong> (NYSE:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/UAL">UAL</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=UAL">Free Report</a>), announced in July the introduction of Boeing 777-300ER service (the airline&rsquo;s latest aircraft type featuring the all-new United Polaris business class seats) to additional routes.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Carriers are also investing substantially toward modernizing their respective fleet. For example, <strong>American Airlines Group</strong> (Nasdaq:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/AAL">AAL</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=AAL">Free Report</a>) invested $1.1 billion in a new aircraft during the second quarter of 2017. In fact, it aims to shell out $4.1 billion in the current year for the same purpose. Moreover, carriers like Delta are looking to reduce their debt levels based on their financial prosperity.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Bullish Readings</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The global traffic data for July, released by the International Air Transport Association (&ldquo;IATA&rdquo;) raises optimism. Load factor (percentage of seats filled by passengers) touched record levels of 84.7% in July. The upside was due to the fact that traffic growth (6.8%) outpaced capacity expansion (6.1%) for the month. The favorable load factor reading highlights the fact that demand for air travel is strong.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Moreover, demand for air freight across the globe witnessed double-digit growth (11.4%) in July. This was, in fact, the fourth month out of five where double-digit demand growth was witnessed. The reading is well above the 10-year average growth rate of 3.1%. With growth in demand outpacing capacity expansion, the scenario bodes well for airline yields.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Traffic growth witnessed by the industry in the first half of 2017 was the highest in 12 years. Load factor also touched record levels. Additionally, at its 73<sup>rd</sup> Annual General Meeting in Cancun, Mexico, IATA stated that airline companies are expected to be more profitable in 2017 than previously expected. IATA now expects global net profit for the industry to come in at $31.4 billion (the earlier projection hinted at profits of $29.8 billion for 2017). The bulk of global profits ($15.4 billion) is expected to come from the North American region.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Traffic data for the first half of 2017 released by the U.S. Department of Transportation&rsquo;s Bureau of Transportation Statistics (BTS) also highlights the bullish case for carriers based in the United States. The BTS data states that a record number of passengers were transported by U.S.-based carriers in the period. The reading for load factor was also favorable.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Moreover, the busy Labor Day travel period (Aug 30-Sep 5) for U.S. airlines this year further highlights that demand for air travel remains strong. This bodes well for airlines.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Other Tailwinds</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">High labor costs have been hurting bottom-line growth for airlines for quite some time. Even though such costs will remain a hindrance, the good news is that the extent of their increase is expected to decline with time.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">For example, American Airlines predicted in September that cost per available seat miles(excluding fuel and special Items) the year-over-year growth is likely to be around 3% in the final quarter of 2017. The metric had grown by 7.6% and 6.8%, respectively, in the first two quarters of 2017. The year-over-year growth for this measure of unit costs is likely to come down further to less than 2% in 2018/19.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Latin American carriers like <strong>GOL Linhas</strong> (NYSE:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/GOL">GOL</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=GOL">Free Report</a>) are seeing better times, buoyed by an improved economy. GOL&rsquo;s view for full-year 2017 is impressive. We expect the company&rsquo;s focus on capacity discipline to result in improvement in yields, going forward. GOL Linhas holds a Zacks Rank #2 (Buy). You can see&nbsp;<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/buy-list/?ADID=zp_1link&amp;ICID=zpi%20_1link" title="blocked::https://www.zacks.com/stocks/buy-list/?ADID=zp_1link&amp;ICID=zpi _1link"><strong>the complete list of today&rsquo;s Zacks #1 Rank (Strong Buy) stocks here</strong></a>.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">European low-cost carrier <strong>Ryanair Holdings</strong> (Nasdaq:<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/RYAAY">RYAAY</a> &ndash; <a href="https://www.zacks.com/registration/pfp/?ALERT=ZR_LINK&amp;adid=PR_AB&amp;d_alert=rd_final_rank&amp;t=RYAAY">Free Report</a>), which is being aided by its customer-friendly &lsquo;Always Getting Better&rsquo; campaign, unveiled a busy London schedule for the summer of 2018, amid Brexit-related fears. The carrier aims to transport 24.8 million customers from three London airports &mdash; Stansted, Gatwick and Luton. With the Greek economy showing signs of revival, exciting times might be in store for Ryanair as it offers multiple flights to the Greek Islands.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>To Wrap Up</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The above commentary clearly suggests that despite headwinds, there exist enough reasons to be bullish about the industry&rsquo;s prospects. Africa business to Switzerland-based diversified resource companyGlencore plc <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/GLNCY">GLNCY</a>. With the deal, Glencore will secure its first major refinery in the continent, in sync with its aim to expand through strategic acquisitions.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Last year, U.S. energy giant Chevron announced plans to unload 75% interests in South Africa assets as part of its three-year divestment goals announced in 2014. In October 2016, energy firms like France&rsquo;s integrated oil and gas major TOTAL S.A. <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/TOT">TOT</a>, Glencore, Russian oil trader Gunvor Group Limited among others had put in bids to snap up stakes in Chevron&rsquo;s South Africa business.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In March, Chevron announced plans to divest the assets to Asia&rsquo;s largest oil refiner, China Petroleum &amp; Chemical Corporation <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/SNP">SNP</a>, also known as Sinopec. However, the deal got stalled due to delays. Concurrently, Chevron&rsquo;s Black Economic Empowerment partners &mdash; who own 25% stake in the South African assets &mdash; reopened the sales process by exercising their pre-emption rights&nbsp;and Glencore was selected due to the better terms and conditions it offered.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Deal Highlights</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Per the deal, Glencore will acquire 75% controlling stake in Chevron&rsquo;s South Africa and Botswana assets including a 100,000 barrel per day oil refinery in Cape Town, a lubricants plant in Durban and a network of around 820 gas stations. The remaining 25% interest will be owned by the consortium of Black Economic Empowerment shareholders. Last year, Chevron earned $138m as pre-tax profits from the South African business unit. Glencore will also remain part of Chevron&rsquo;s management team and workforce from its South African business unit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The divestment deal is valued at $973 million and is subject to approval by regulatory authorities. It will help Chevron to slash costs and streamline business models.&nbsp;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">For Glencore &mdash; which already has extensive portfolio of assets in South Africa &mdash; the current acquisition is likely to strategically complement its existing assets and provide a lucrative downstream opportunity. implementing an electrode surcharge for all stainless product shipments effective Oct 29.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The move is in response to the recent significant hike in cost of graphite electrodes, which is used by the company to produce stainless steel grades in steelmaking operations. &nbsp;&nbsp;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">According to AK Steel, the monthly electrode surcharge amount will be listed in the company\'s monthly surcharge publication. The amount will also be same for all stainless grades produced by the company. For November 2017, electrode surcharge amount for shipments will be $13.20 per ton.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Shares of AK Steelhave declined 7% in the last three months, underperforming the <a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/industry-rank/industry/stel-producers-176">industry</a>&rsquo;s 6.5% growth.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">&nbsp;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><img alt="" src="https://staticx-tuner.zacks.com/images/zadmin_tuner_image/aks_2017_10_09.jpg" style="width: 620px; height: 277px;" /></p><p style="text-align: justify;">&nbsp;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AK Steel, during second-quarter 2017 earnings call, declared that it expects shipments in the third quarter to be relatively flat compared to the second as higher shipments of the carbon distributing and converting market are expected to be offset by lower automotive shipments. Average selling price in the third quarter is expected to be modestly lower than the second quarter. The expected decline assumes a change in the mix of shipments related to an anticipated reduction in automotive shipments and decline in raw material surcharges.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AK Steel is expected to benefit from the strengthening in the automotive market. The company is currently developing third-generation, advanced high-strength carbon steels for its automotive customers that are considerably stronger than current product offerings.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Moreover, the recently completed acquisition of Precision Partners is in sync with AK Steel\'s commitment to broaden its portfolio of high-value products and processes and also advances the company&rsquo;s focus on the rapidly growing automotive lightweighting industry and its position in advanced high strength steels. Prior to this, the company received Parts Manufacturer Approval from the Federal Aviation Administration for this windshield, following which its demand by U.S. operators grew steadily. With the latest EASA approval, the company is now able to offer this product to European operators.<br /><br />The newly designed windshield provides superior scratch, abrasion and chemical resistance along with an improved, more reliable anti-ice heating system, higher visible light transmittance and improved precipitation-static drain. u'<p>The projected decline in <strong>JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co.</strong>&rsquo;s <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/JPM">JPM</a> trading revenue will likely deal a major blow to its third-quarter earnings given significant dependence of its top line on this source. But this might not lead the company to report dismal results on Oct 12. Benefits of higher rates, decent loan growth and relatively better performance of the other segments &mdash; particularly investment banking &mdash; may overshadow the trading gloom.<br /><br />The stock, which recently showed strength on investors&rsquo; optimism over potential tax reforms as well as the Fed&rsquo;s plans to unwind its giant balance sheet and keep increasing interest rates, may not take a hit due to the damage caused by the slump in trading revenue. This is because the bad news has already been factored out.<br /><br />Moreover, though market volatility has not improved much since last quarter, the huge year-over-year decline in trading revenue &mdash; highest since 2011 &mdash; will primarily be attributable to comparison with a quarter, which had witnessed higher-than-usual volatility due to the Brexit aftermath and the impending U.S. presidential election.<br /><br />While the momentum in investment banking business is likely to continue, growth in commercial and industrial loans as well as consumer lending should lend support to revenues.<br /><br />However, we do not expect major support from lower expenses to the bottom line this time around, as JPMorgan doesn&rsquo;t have enough scope to reduce expenses further. If fact, there were some legal expenses in the quarter.<br /><br />While the Zacks Consensus Estimate for earnings has not been revised over the last seven days, the trend over the last 30 days depict pessimism. The Zacks Consensus Estimate for the to-be-reported quarter has been revised 1.2% downward over the last 30 days to $1.67, with four out of eight estimates moving lower and one moving higher. However, the Zacks Consensus Estimate reflects a year-over-year improvement of 5.6%.<br /><br />Decreasing earnings estimates increase the chance of a beat. The latest launch is expected to boost the segment&rsquo;scontribution.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Integra&rsquo;s efforts to grow in the plastic and reconstructive surgery market seem to be strategic as per Technavio data published in Business Wire. Per the report, the global plastic surgery products market is expected to reach a value of around $15 billion, at a CAGR of 9% between 2016 and 2020.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">We believe growing consciousness about appearance among individuals, increasing awareness and rising expenditure in healthcare and technological advancements are likely to drive demand for cosmetic surgeries. 5.4pt;mso-para-margin-top:0in;mso-para-margin-right:0in;mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;mso-para-margin-left:0in;line-height:115%;mso-pagination:widow-orphan;font-size:11.0pt;font-family:"Calibri","sans-serif";mso-ascii-font-family:Calibri;mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}</style><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;">Earnings growth enthralls almost everyone, right from the top brass to research analysts. But the question here is why? If the company doesn&rsquo;t make money, it won&rsquo;t stand the test of time. Take a company&rsquo;s revenues over a given period of time, subtract the cost of production and you will have its earnings!</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;">This metric is also considered to be the most noteworthy variable in influencing the share price. Better-than-expected earnings performances normally lead to a rally in the share price. However, in addition to actual earnings, expectations of earnings play a significant role in influencing the price of a stock.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b>Earnings Estimates Determine Share Prices</b></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;">We have often seen a decline in the stock price despite earnings growth and a rally in the price following an earnings decline. This is largely a result of a company&rsquo;s earnings failing to meet market expectations.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;">Earnings estimates embody analysts&rsquo; opinions of factors such as sales growth, product demand, competitive industry environment, profit margins and cost control. Thus, earnings estimates serve as a valuable tool while making investment decisions. Earnings estimates also help analysts assess the cash flow to determine the fair value of a firm.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;">Investors, thus, should be on the lookout for stocks that are ready to make a big move. Hence, it is important for investors to buy stocks that have historical earnings growth and are also seeing a rise in quarterly and annual earnings estimates.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b>The Winning Strategy</b></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;">In order to shortlist stocks that have striking earnings growth and positive estimate revisions, we have added the following parameters:</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span>Zacks Rank less than or equal to 2 </span></strong>(Only Zacks\' \'Buys\' and \'Strong Buys\' are allowed. With the Zacks Rank proving itself to be one of the best rating systems out there, this is a great way to start things off.) You can see <a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/buy-list/?ADID=zp_1link&amp;ICID=zpi%20_1link"><strong><span>the complete list of today&rsquo;s Zacks #1 Rank (Strong Buy) stocks here</span></strong></a>.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span>5-Year Historical EPS Growth (%) greater than X-Industry </span></strong>(Stocks that possess strong EPS growth history.)</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span>% Change EPS F(0)/F(-1) greater than or equal to 5 </span></strong>(Companies that witnessed year-over-year earnings growth rate of 5% or more in the last reported fiscal.)</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span>% Change Q1 Estimates over the last 4 weeks greater than zero </span></strong>(Stocks that have seen their current quarter earnings estimates revised higher in the last 4 weeks.)</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span>% Change F1 Estimates over the last 1 week greater than zero </span></strong>(Stocks that have seen their annual earnings estimates revised higher in the last 1 week.)</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span>% Change F1 Estimates over the last 4 weeks greater than zero </span></strong>(Stocks that have seen their annual earnings estimates revised higher in the last 4 weeks.)</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;">The above criteria narrowed down the universe of around 7,818 stocks to only 23. Among them, we have selected five large-cap stocks. Such stocks have long-term performance history and are more stable than what mid-caps or small caps offer. Companies with market capitalization of more than $10 billion are generally considered large cap.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;">Here are the top five stocks:</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b>Facebook Inc</b> <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/FB">FB</a> is focused on building products that enable people to connect and share through mobile devices, personal computers and other surfaces. The company&rsquo;s products include Facebook, Instagram, Messenger, WhatsApp and Oculus. Facebook has a Zacks Rank #2 (Buy). The company&rsquo;s estimated growth rate for this year is 26.5%, higher than the <a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/industry-rank/industry/internet-services-213">industry</a>&rsquo;s gain of 13.7%.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b>NVIDIA Corporation</b> <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/NVDA">NVDA</a> focuses on personal computer (PC) graphics, graphics processing unit (GPU) and also on artificial intelligence (AI). The company operates through two segments: GPU and Tegra Processor. NVIDIA has a Zacks Rank #1 (Strong Buy). The company&rsquo;s estimated growth rate for this year is 40.5%, higher than the <a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/industry-rank/industry/semiconductor-general-241">industry</a>&rsquo;s gain of 24.8%.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b>Principal Financial Group Inc</b> <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/PFG">PFG</a> is an investment management company. The company offers a range of financial products and services, including retirement, asset management and insurance. Principal Financial has a Zacks Rank #2. The company&rsquo;s estimated growth rate for this year is 14.4%, higher than the <a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/industry-rank/industry/financial-investment-management-63">industry</a>&rsquo;s gain of 8.1%.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b>A. O. Smith Corp</b> <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/AOS">AOS</a> manufactures and markets residential and commercial gas, electric water heaters, and water treatment products in North America, China, Europe, and India. The company has a Zacks Rank #2. The company&rsquo;s estimated growth rate for this year is 14%, higher than the <a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/industry-rank/industry/manufacturing-electronics-97">industry</a>&rsquo;s gain of 6.6%.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b>Lincoln National Corporation</b> <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/LNC">LNC</a> is a holding company, which operates insurance and retirement businesses through subsidiary companies. The company has a Zacks Rank #2. The company&rsquo;s estimated growth rate for this year is 14.7%, higher than the <a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/industry-rank/industry/insurance-life-insurance-87">industry</a>&rsquo;s gain of 12.6%.</p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;">You can get the rest of the stocks on this list by signing up now for your 2-week free trial to the Research Wizard and start using this screen in your own trading. This is especially evident if you look to recent earnings estimates for the stock.</span></span></p><p><span style="font-size: 16px;"><span style="font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;">For the current quarter, we have seen eight estimates go lower for earnings in the past month compared to zero higher, while we have seen a similar trend for the current year as well. After all, JetBlue accounts for roughly a third of passengers at the airport, so it is likely to have a visible impact on operations.</span></p><p><span style="font-size: 16px;"><span style="font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;">Take all these factors together and it shouldn&rsquo;t be a surprise that JBLU has a Zacks Rank #5 (Strong Sell) and why we are looking for a return to sluggish trading in this company in the near future.</span></span></p><p><span style="font-size: 16px;"><span style="font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;"><strong>Other Choices</strong></span></span></p><p><span style="font-size: 16px;"><span style="font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;">Clearly, JetBlue is a choice to consider avoiding this fall in the airline space. But what are some better picks for investors in today&rsquo;s climate?</span></span></p><p><span style="font-size: 16px;"><span style="font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;">Well, a good idea might be to consider transport companies outside of the airline space. Get Bumpier for Airline Stocks?', 'language': None}, 'published_parsed': time.struct_time(tm_year=2017, tm_mon=10, tm_mday=6, tm_hour=21, tm_min=46, tm_sec=0, tm_wday=4, tm_yday=279, tm_isdst=0), 'links': [{'href': u'http://www.zacks.com/commentary/131256/will-the-ride-get-bumpier-for-airline-stocks?cid=CS-ZC-FT-131256', 'type': u'text/html', 'rel': u'alternate'}], 'title': u'Will the Ride Get Bumpier for Airline Stocks?', 'authors': [{'name': u'Zacks Equity Research'}, {'name': u'Zacks Equity Research'}], 'summary': u'Will the Ride Get Bumpier for Airline Stocks?', 'content': [{'base': u'http://feed.zacks.com/commentary/AllStories/rss', 'type': u'text/html', 'value': u'<p>It is a well-documented fact that stocks in the airline space have been plagued by multiple headwinds like weather-related disruptions, pricing issues and high costs. The turbulence in the sector is largely responsible for the NYSE ARCA Airline Index declining 2.5% over the last three months. With Q3 earnings season coming up, the ongoing turbulence may result in airlines performing disappointingly. Let&rsquo;s delve into the details.</p><p><strong>Harvey, Irma Ground Airlines - Q3 Unit Revenue Views Cut</strong></p><p>Harvey, which wreaked havoc on America&rsquo;s fourth-largest city, Houston, with heavy rainfall, has negatively impacted airline operations and caused multiple flight cancellations. In fact, air travel was hurt with two Houston airports, George Bush Intercontinental Airport (IAH) and William P. Hobby Airport (HOU), <a href="https://www.bizjournals.com/houston/news/2017/08/30/southwest-cancels-more-flights-houston-airports.html?ana=yahoo&amp;yptr=yahoo">reportedly</a> remaining closed for a few days (since the noon of Aug 27) due to Harvey-induced heavy rainfall. The airports are operational now.</p><p>United Continental Holdings (<acronym class="ticker">UAL</acronym>), the parent company of United Airlines, was the worst hit, as Houston is the carrier&rsquo;s second-largest hub. In September 2017, company trimmed its views with respect to pre-tax margin and passenger revenue per available seat mile (PRASM: a key measure of unit revenue) for the third quarter mainly due to Harvey. The carrier now expects PRASM to decline between 3% and 5% year over year (the earlier guidance provided in July was +1% to - 1%).</p><p>In fact, Harvey has impacted the third-quarter PRASM to the tune of approximately 150 basis points. The carrier now expects pre-tax margin between 8% and 10% (previous guidance was 12.5% and 14.5%).</p><p>Spirit Airlines (<acronym class="ticker">SAVE</acronym>), which also has significant exposure to Houston, expects its top line to shrink to the tune of approximately $8.5 million in the third quarter due to the natural calamity. Currently, Spirit Airlines anticipates total revenue per available seat mile (TRASM) to decline between 7% and 8.5% (the previous guidance was 2% and 4%). In fact, per the company, 100 basis points of the trimmed guidance can be attributed to the negative impact of Harvey. Also, aggressive competitive pricing in its key markets contributed to the bleak forecast.</p><p>Southwest Airlines (LUV), which had to call off approximately 2,800 flights due to Harvey, now expects operating revenue per available seat mile (RASM) for the third quarter in the range of down 1% to slightly up, on a year-over-year basis. The metric was earlier projected to increase approximately 1% from the year-ago quarter.</p><p>Close on the heels of Harvey, came another natural calamity, Irma, which also hurt airline operations. American Airlines Group (<acronym class="ticker">AAL</acronym>), which has significant exposure to Florida including its hub at Miami International Airport, had to cancel multiple flights due to Irma. The natural calamity also caused it to trim its third-quarter TRASM view.</p><p><strong>High Costs Likely to Hurt Q3</strong></p><p>With labor deals in vogue in the aviation space, labor costs have escalated, thereby hurting the bottom lines in the last few quarters. The picture is likely to be no different in the third quarter.&nbsp; For example, labor costs shot up significantly at Alaska Air Group (<acronym class="ticker">ALK</acronym>) following the amendment to the pay-related pilots&rsquo; contract at its subsidiary, Horizon Air.</p><p>Following the agreement, the company&nbsp;expects third-quarter cost per available seat mile (excluding fuel and other special items) between 8 cents and 8.05 cents. High labor costs are also expected to hurt results at Allegiant Travel Company (<acronym class="ticker">ALGT</acronym>). Allegiant carries a Zacks Rank #3 (Hold). You can see&nbsp;<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/buy-list/?ADID=zp_1link&amp;ICID=zpi%20_1link" title="blocked::https://www.zacks.com/stocks/buy-list/?ADID=zp_1link&amp;ICID=zpi _1link"><strong>the complete list of today&rsquo;s Zacks #1 Rank (Strong Buy) stocks here</strong></a>.</p><p>Moreover, increasing fuel costs do not bode well for airlines. Oil prices are currently hovering around the $50-a-barrel mark, way higher than the lows of around $26 a barrel touched in February last year. The rise in fuel costs, which again may be Harvey induced, are also likely to distort the Q3 earnings picture for airlines. For example, Delta Air Lines (<acronym class="ticker">DAL</acronym>) now expects fuel prices per gallon in the third quarter between $1.68 and $1.73. The figure was much less in the second quarter of 2017.</p><p><strong>Capacity Overexpansion &amp; Declining Airfare</strong></p><p>Carriers like Spirit Airlines and JetBlue Airways Corp. (JBLU) registered declines in their respective load factors (percentage of seats filled by passengers) in August. The reason for the downturn was capacity expansion outweighing traffic growth in the month. The metric had declined for most carriers in July as well.</p><p>Woes related to capacity overexpansion plagued airline stocks in the not so distant past (particularly 2015) also. In light of the above traffic reports, it is quite natural for fears related to capacity overexpansion to resurface.</p><p>In such a scenario, investors fear that capacity expansion may lead to oversupply in the market even as fuel costs remain well below the highs of mid-2014, despite the recent resurgence (jet fuel prices climbed 8.5% in August). Moreover, airfares have remained low, with the metric declining in August as well after the fall in July.</p><p>According to <a href="http://www.hopper.com/research/airfare-close-to-bottoming-out-for-the-season">research firm Hopper</a>, air fares (roundtrip) in the United States are likely hit a low of $216 in October. Capacity over-expansion is believed to be the primary reason for the decline in airfares. While low air fares are favorable for fliers, it is a drag on the top lines of carriers due to their lesser profits.</p><p><strong>Threat from Low-Cost Carriers</strong></p><p>The emergence and success of low-cost carriers like Spirit Airlines and JetBlue Airways have posed significant threats to legacy carriers. In a price-sensitive economy, it is not only a question of the survival of the fittest but also of the cheapest. In fact, United Continental, while trimming its guidance for the third quarter attributed the move to its price war with carriers like Spirit apart from Harvey and high fuel costs.</p><p>United Continental and American Airlines introduced Basic Economy Fares earlier this year to attract more budget-conscious passengers. Recently, American Airlines announced its decision to expand basic economy fares to more domestic flights in a bid to compete more effectively with low-cost carriers.</p><p><strong>Other Headwinds</strong></p><p>In July 2017, American Airlines, Frontier Airlines and Delta were heavily fined by the U.S. Department of Transportation (DOT) for flouting rules pertaining to consumer protection. The DOT fined Frontier Airlines $400,000 for breach rules pertaining to oversales and disability. American Airlines was penalized to the tune of $250,000 as it failed to make timely refunds to passengers. Delta was fined $200,000 by the agency for revealing inaccurate baggage-related reports.</p><p>United Airlines, the subsidiary of United Continental, again grabbed headlines in July owing to passenger harassment issues, following the infamous David Dao episode in April. This time, the carrier <a href="http://miami.cbslocal.com/2017/07/06/united-air-facing-backlash-for-bumping-toddler-from-his-seat/">reportedly</a> forced a passenger, Shirley Yamauchi, on a flight from Houston to Boston, to remove her 27-month son from his seat, the ticket for which had cost almost <a href="http://www.hawaiinewsnow.com/story/35811846/hawaii-teacher-forced-to-hold-son-on-lap-after-united-gives-purchased-seat-to-standby-passenger">$1,000</a>. The toddler had to sit on his mother&rsquo;s lap during the course of the journey while his paid seat was given to another passenger.</p><p>The twin terror attacks in Spain, in August 2017, also do not bode well for airlines. Such acts of terrorism affect airline stocks as there is a possibility of waning travel demand due to security fears. Moreover, as a result of mass shooting in Las Vegas, travel to this favorite tourist destination might be hurt. As a result, travel-focused stocks, which include airlines, are likely to be on the back foot.</p><p>Moreover, technical glitches have been a nuisance for carriers. Evidently, the likes of Delta and Southwest Airlines have seen their operations being affected by technological problems this year. Given that technological infrastructure is a key expense for airlines, the profitability of carriers might be affected in the event of such malfunctions, going forward.</p><p>Check out our latest <a href="https://www.zacks.com/commentary/131006/airline-industry-outlook---october-2017">Airline Industry Outlook</a> for more news on the current state of affairs in this market from an earnings perspective, and how the trend looks for this important sector at the moment.</p><p><strong>Can Hackers Put Money INTO Your Portfolio?<br /><br /></strong>Earlier this month, credit bureau Equifax announced a massive data breach affecting 2 out of every 3 Americans. u'<p>The U.S. economy has been witnessing significant demographic changes with aging and retiring baby-boomer generation. This should lead to significant increase in demand for healthcare services. As a result, healthcare real estate investment trusts (REIT) could thrive.<br /><br />The senior citizen population has been growing at a faster rate than any other generation. In fact, according to the Census Bureau, the number of citizens with more than 85 years of age is estimated to reach 8.7 million by 2030. Moreover, as senior citizens end up spending more on healthcare services as compared to the average population, healthcare spending is projected to grow annually at a rate of 5.8% over the 2014-2024 period &mdash; according to recently published government data.<br /><br />As one of the largest generational group in the United States, baby boomers constitute a major customer base of healthcare services. We believe the &ldquo;silver tsunami&rdquo; &mdash; the rising senior citizens&rsquo; population &mdash; will offer abundant upside potential for healthcare REITs.<br /><br />Further, the increasing longevity has encouraged these REITs to invest in hospitals, medical office buildings (MOB) and senior housing facilities. MOBs offer low-cost medical services and are subsequently enjoying impressive top-line growth.<br /><br />Healthcare REITs are rotating capital out of high-cost hospitals and investing in low-cost facilities. Since skilled nursing facilities (SNFs) are becoming more susceptible to top-line pressure due to changes in medical billing procedure, companies are reducing exposure to this asset class.<br /><br />The strategy of healthcare companies to emphasize on private-pay models provides ample room for growth in this relatively fragmented market.<br />&nbsp;<br />Although the healthcare REIT sector has been burdened with oversupply of senior housing assets at present, we expect demand to catch up with an improvement in absorption rates.<br /><br />As there is ample scope for growth with aging Americans, the following healthcare REITs can be solid bets.<br /><br /><strong>3 Stocks to Consider</strong><br /><br /><strong>Sabra Healthcare REIT, Inc.</strong> <a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/SBRA">SBRA</a> is a healthcare REIT that owns nursing homes, rehabilitation centers, assisted living facilities and independent living centers. The stock currently sports a Zacks Rank #1 (Strong Buy). The company&rsquo;s year-over-year funds from operation (FFO) and revenue growth are estimated at 163.6% and 49.1%, respectively, for 2017.<br />&nbsp;<br />Moreover, the company boosts ROE of 8.72%, higher than the industry average of 5.96%.<br /><br />You can see <strong><a href="https://www.zacks.com/stocks/buy-list?adid=ZP_quote_ribbon_1list&amp;icid=zpi_quote_ribbon_1list">the complete list of today&rsquo;s Zacks #1 Rank stocks here.</a><br /><br />National Health Investors, Inc. </strong><a href="http://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/NHI">NHI</a> is a healthcare REIT which invests in healthcare-related facilities, including long-term care facilities, acute care hospitals, medical office buildings, retirement centers and assisted living facilities. The company also holds a Zacks Rank of 2. u'http://www.zacks.com/commentary/131254/are-bank-stock-gains-sustainable?cid=CS-ZC-FT-131254', 'type': u'text/html', 'rel': u'alternate'}], 'title': u'Are Bank Stock Gains Sustainable?', 'authors': [{'name': u'Sheraz Mian'}, {'name': u'Sheraz Mian'}], 'summary': u'Are Bank Stock Gains Sustainable?', 'content': [{'base': u'http://feed.zacks.com/commentary/AllStories/rss', 'type': u'text/html', 'value': u'<p>It has been a tough ride for bank stocks this year, with the industry unable to sustain the post-election momentum after mid-February 2017. As a group, bank stocks didn&rsquo;t do much from mid-February through early September. But they have experienced dramatic gains since September 8th, with a number of major bank stocks trading at or near their highs for the year.<br /><br />This lack of sustained performance notwithstanding, the industry remains an integral part of the &lsquo;Trump Trade&rsquo;, with the industry handily outperforming the broader market since November 7th.<br /><br />The chart below plots the performance of the Zacks Major Banks industry relative to the S&amp;P 500 Index since the elections. Please note that the Zacks Major Banks industry includes all the money-center banks and big regionals that kick-off the Q3 earnings season for the industry on Thursday October 12th with the <strong>JPMorgan</strong> (<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/jpm">JPM</a>) and <strong>Citigroup</strong> (<a href="https://www.zacks.com/stock/quote/c">C</a>) results.</p><p><img alt="" src="https://staticx-tuner.zacks.com/images/zadmin_tuner_image/10_6_17 1.jpg" style="width: 620px; height: 292px;" /></p><p>What this chart (blue line represents the banking group) shows is that stocks in the Zacks Major Banks industry are up +28.5% since November 7th, outperforming the S&amp;P 500 index&rsquo;s +19.2% gain in that same time period. The broader Finance sector, of which the Major Banks industry is big part, accounting for roughly 40% of the sector&rsquo;s total earnings, is up +24% since November 7th.<br /><br />Bank stocks are up more than +8% over the past month, roughly double the S&amp;P 500&rsquo;s performance in that time period. Optimism about tax policy changes appears to be a contributing factor to the group&rsquo;s recent momentum. It&rsquo;s hard to be overly optimistic about substance and timing of a policy legislation given the healthcare experience, but lower corporate taxes will be highly beneficial to the banking industry. As large as many of these big industry players are, they are still primarily domestic oriented businesses that stand to benefit from lower corporate tax rates (just as small-cap stocks do).<br /><br />Trends in treasury yields have an outsized bearing on bank stocks since they are a big driver of bank margins. You can see this correlation in the year-to-date stock market performance of the industry relative to the 10-year treasury yield (bank industry is blue line), with the industry&rsquo;s bounce since September 8th coinciding with the most recent bottoming in the treasury yields.</p><p><img alt="" src="https://staticx-tuner.zacks.com/images/zadmin_tuner_image/10_6_17 2.jpg" style="width: 620px; height: 325px;" /></p><p>Whether the group&rsquo;s recent outperformance over the past month is a function of treasury yields, or hopes of tax law changes or both, it&rsquo;s foundations appear shaky. Tax cuts would be good for banks, but who knows when or whether they will arrive. Treasury yields have been unable to cross the 2.4% level at the high end, though they reached that level three times since March this year. They are heading to that level again, with the 10-year yield getting a modest bump from the stronger-looking wage growth numbers in the otherwise &lsquo;noisy&rsquo; September jobs report. But if recent history has to repeat itself, then we should look for yields to start moving down after getting close to the 2.4% level. &nbsp;<br /><br />With these two supports for the group less than credible, let&rsquo;s take a look at the group&rsquo;s earnings potential to see if we can find support there.<br /><br /><strong>What Are Banks Expected to Report in Q3?</strong><br /><br />Bank earnings failed to impress in the Q2 earnings season and all of the factors that weighed on Q2 results remained in place in Q3 as well, keeping expectations in check. Net interest margin benefited from the June Fed rate hike, but that incremental gain likely got offset by persistent deceleration in loan growth and soft trading revenues. The September quarter is traditionally a seasonally weak period on the capital markets front. This year&rsquo;s Q3 was mixed, with stable fixed income trading flows and positive fixed income underwriting trends offset by weak equity trading volumes and issuance.<br /><br />What all of this means is that bank stocks could benefit from low and relatively easy-to-beat expectations.<br /><br />Total Q3 earnings for the Zacks Major Banks industry are expected to be down -5.1% from the same period last year on +2.2% higher revenues. This would follow +10% earnings growth in Q2 and +19.4% growth in 2017 Q2. JP Morgan (JPM) and Citigroup (C), on deck to release Q3 results on Thursday, are expected to report -6.6% and -8.2% lower earnings from the year-earlier level, respectively.<br /><br />The table below shows the sector&rsquo;s Q3 earnings growth expectations at the medium-industry level contrasted with estimates for the following four quarters and actual results for the preceding three periods.</p><p><img alt="" src="https://staticx-tuner.zacks.com/images/zadmin_tuner_image/10_6_17 3.jpg" style="width: 620px; height: 160px;" /></p><p>Please note that the Major Banks industry, of which JPMorgan, Citigroup and others are part, accounts for roughly 45% of the sector&rsquo;s total earnings (insurance is the second biggest earnings contributor, accounting for about 25% of the total). The insurance industry has been hard hit by this year&rsquo;s very active and impactful hurricane season, with estimates for insurers taking a big hit since the quarter got underway.<br /><br />We discussed the hurricane impact in our weekly Earnings Trends report here &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;<a href="https://www.zacks.com/commentary/131005/the-earnings-impact-of-hurricanes">Earnings Impact of Hurricanes</a></p><p><strong>Expectations for Q3</strong><br /><br />Total Q3 earnings are expected to be up +2.2% from the same period last year on +5% higher revenues. This would follow +11.1% earnings growth in 2017 Q2 on +5.5%, the second quarter in a row of double-digit earnings growth.<br /><br />Estimates for Q3 came down as the quarter unfolded, with the current +2.2% growth down from +6.3% at the end of June. The chart below shows how Q3 earnings growth expectations have evolved since the start of the quarter.</p><p><img alt="" src="https://staticx-tuner.zacks.com/images/zadmin_tuner_image/10_6_17 4.jpg" style="width: 620px; height: 389px;" /></p><p>Please note that while Q3 estimates have followed the well traversed path that we have been seeing consistently over the last few years, the magnitude of negative revisions nevertheless compares favorably to other periods. In other words, Q3 estimates have come down, but they haven&rsquo;t come down by as much.<br /><br />The table below shows the summary picture for Q3, contrasted with what was actually achieved in Q2.</p><p><img alt="" src="https://staticx-tuner.zacks.com/images/zadmin_tuner_image/10_6_17 5.jpg" style="width: 620px; height: 686px;" /></p><p>In terms of sector focus, the strongest growth in Q3 is coming from the Energy sector which benefits from easy comparisons. Excluding the Energy sector, the aggregate growth pace drops to +0.4% from +2.2%. The Conglomerate sector is the only other sectors with double-digit growth rates. Earnings growth is also strong for the Technology sector, with total earnings for the sector expected to be up +9.7% on +6.7% higher revenues.<br /><br />On the negative side, Q3 earnings are expected to be below the year-earlier level for 8 of the 16 Zacks sectors, with double-digit declines for the Transportation, Aerospace, Basic Materials and Autos sectors.<br /><br />The chart below shows Q3 earnings growth expectations contrasted with what is expected in the following three quarters and actual results in the preceding 5 quarters. As you can see in the chart below, the growth pace has started decelerating from the double-digit level of the first two quarters of the year.</p><p><img alt="" src="https://staticx-tuner.zacks.com/images/zadmin_tuner_image/10_6_17 6.jpg" style="width: 620px; height: 390px;" /></p><p>The chart below shows the weekly reporting calendar for the S&amp;P 500 index. As you can see, we have only 8 index members reporting results this week, with the earnings season really ramping up the following week.</p><p><img alt="" src="https://staticx-tuner.zacks.com/images/zadmin_tuner_image/10_6_17 7.jpg" style="width: 620px; height: 244px;" /></p><p><em>Note: Sheraz Mian manages the Zacks equity research department.
